<div id="review_1082002600" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1082002600" />
    <a title="destini mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia"><img alt="destini mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499903277p2/13742215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1082002600?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destini mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destini mia" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia">destini mia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13742215-destini-mia?shelf=the-holy-grail">the-holy-grail</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1082002600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10568255705057504087"><i>
  <blockquote>He said, “I think it’s time to find Glendower.”<br/>Adam said, “I think you’re right.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><b>YAYYY!! It's out now and I'm so excited to relive TRK through everyone else's eyes ♥</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870680.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870681.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870682.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870683.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870684.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm sitting here now trying to string some decent words together, with dried tears on my cheeks, in hopes of being able to convey even a shred of the feelings warring inside me. <br/><br/>For three books, I have tried to describe exactly what this series means to me. And in those three attempts, I feel as if I have failed. At this point, <b>i</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10568255705057504087" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>He said, “I think it’s time to find Glendower.”<br>Adam said, “I think you’re right.”</blockquote>
</i><br><b>YAYYY!! It's out now and I'm so excited to relive TRK through everyone else's eyes ♥</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870680.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870681.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870682.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870683.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461465931i/18870684.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm sitting here now trying to string some decent words together, with dried tears on my cheeks, in hopes of being able to convey even a shred of the feelings warring inside me. <br><br>For three books, I have tried to describe exactly what this series means to me. And in those three attempts, I feel as if I have failed. At this point, <b>its beyond words</b>. It's more than happiness and sadness and the overwhelming feeling of wonder. <b>It's all those things and none of those things and five starts just doesn't seem like enough</b>. <br><br>Maggie Stiefvater has a way with words. Words that I've known for most my life and learned to string together. She manages to make something <i>more</i> of them. She fashions it into a story, and makes it sound like poetry. <b>She takes everything you've ever felt and gives it a name</b>. <br><br><i>The Raven King</i> makes your heart pound and makes your heart stop. It makes you laugh and makes you have an impromptu sob session at 12:47am. The characters are <b>everything</b>, the story is <b>everything</b> and whatever the first three books were, <i>The Raven King</i> was <u>more</u>.<br><i>
  <blockquote>Outside of Henrietta, nestled on the ley line, something dark watched all this, everything in the Henrietta night, and said, I’m awake I’m awake I’m awake.</blockquote>
</i><br>Everything is finally unraveling and coming together. This is definitely the creepiest book of them all. I'm a visual person, so I wouldn't exactly say I was <i>scared</i>. I mean, I was scared for Gansey's life and the state of my ships, but I wasn't scared in that horror movie kind of way. <u>Because I'm a visual person</u>. If this had been made into a movie of something, I would have been shitting myself into oblivion. If these things were <b>actually</b> happening to me, my ass would have been dead before Gansey could say Excelsior. However, I recognize creepiness when I read it, and this was <b>creepy™</b>. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“We should all be afraid,” Noah said, his voice thing through the buzzing. “When you play with time –”</blockquote>
</i><br>...you get Nightmare Fuel. Let's just call it what it is. <br><i>
  <blockquote>He was a king. <br>This was the year he was going to die.</blockquote>
</i><br>TRK almost didn't feel real to me. I honestly, could hardly believe that I had the fourth and final book in my hand. I've never met a famous person, but I feel like it would be a lot like this. Like you just can't believe the person you've been watching on TV and seeing in magazines is actually in front of you, shaking your hand and asking if you'd like a picture. I couldn't believe that I was reading new content. In the beginning, I would just get a little jolt and think, wait... I haven't read this before. Because everything I new was from the first three books and it just wouldn't hit me that after months of wait and following Stiefvater's updates it was here.<br><i>
  <blockquote>Blue was filled with frustration that her life was so clearly demarcated. <br>Things that were not enough, but that she could have. <br>Things that were something more, that she couldn’t.</blockquote>
</i><br><b>It's almost too easy to be spellbound</b>. The characters become dear to you-- I mean, who can't relate to someone who's alway dreamt of <i>more</i>, or of being autonomous, or of being respected, or of being loved. You can easily find a bit of yourself in each character, or a bit of someone you want to become. Your mind buzzes with the characters and the endless possibilities. Of the fact that Gansey is going to die and two kisses have been written into the story and nothing will ever be like it once was. <br><i>
  <blockquote>Making Ronan Lynch smile felt as charged as making a bargain with Cabeswater. These weren’t forces to play with.</blockquote>
</i><br>Which brings me my next topic: THE SHIPS. Oh, the ships. Oh, my heart. I think the fact that Maggie Stiefvater wrote two kisses in <i>The Raven King</i> says enough.<br><br>Well, <b>it really doesn't</b>. <br><br>But that's all you'll get out of me. Its glory can't be replicated in a review, only experienced. Or non-glory. As I said, nothing from me. <br><br>Something Maggie Stiefvater wrote: <i>I am really, really looking forward to the 26th, guys. I hope you love it or hate it, nothing in between.</i><br>Any author that encourages their readers to feel passionate about their story, whether it's passionately loving it or passionately hating it, is an author for me. <b>Because the whole Raven Cycle experience just doesn't stop or begin with the books.</b> The author and the fandom have been a huge part in making this an incredible adventure. With the fan art and the author's willingness to answer questions and interact with readers, it's difficult not to leave with a sense of excitement and satisfaction. <br><br>But more than anything, something Maggie Stiefvater wrote on her blog struck me the hardest. It was her reminder while she was writing the series. <b>The worst thing that could happen to the characters is that they stop being friends</b>. And while I was here worried for them individually or worried about them in their respective ships, I had never really thought about that. But I was hit with how true it was. Because what I <b>couldn't stand</b> more than <i>anything</i>, more than Gansey dying, Pynch not happening, or Henrietta falling off the face of <i>The Raven Cycle</i> planet, was <b>them not being friends anymore</b>. Because more than anything, this is a story about friends. Friends and magic. Would this be much without it?<br><br>I am just going to finish with this: <b>Maggie Stiefvater is pressing down on the ORBMASTER that is my heart.</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>Depending on where you began the story, it was about this place: the long stretch of mountain that straddled a particularly potent segment of the ley line.</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>.::MY REVIEW FOR::.</b><br>⚬ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1596781061?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> (book 1)<br>⚬ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/923246864?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dream Thieves</a> (book 2)<br>⚬ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/924090305?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a> (book 3)<br><br><i>((f.d: the visuals above were edited by myself-- base images were found on google))</i><br><br>________________________<br><br><b>.::UPDATE::.</b> (4/05/16)<br><br>⚬ Prologue &amp; Chapter One can be found <a href="http://buzz.publishersmarketplace.com/book/the-raven-king#tab2" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!<br><br>⚬ Prologue &amp; Chapter One read by Will Patton + Song by Maggie Stiefvater can be heard <a href="https://soundcloud.com/maggie_stiefvater/sets/the-raven-king" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!<br><br><b>UPDATE</b> (2/15/15)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424038041i/13707322.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Gansey x Blue kissing → *cries*<br>Ronan x Adam kissing → *crying intensifies* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>And to clerify:</b> <br>(i'm not making this up, i am actually quoting) <br><br><b>question/statement</b>: maggie, please don't make one of the two kisses that happens just a dream kiss<br>(<a href="http://janesyre.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">source</a>)<br><br><b>maggie</b>: I understand the fandom is full of trepidation due to <a href="http://www.dailydot.com/fandom/bbc-sherlock-watson-gay-club-scene-cut/" rel="nofollow noopener">a</a> <a href="http://www.tvguide.com/news/supernatural-queerbaiting-destiel-1089286/" rel="nofollow noopener">million and one</a> <a href="http://fandomsandfeminism.tumblr.com/post/37116303807/sherlock-is-the-grossest-example-of-queerbaiting" rel="nofollow noopener">instances of baiting</a> <a href="http://groupthink.jezebel.com/lets-talk-about-queer-baiting-on-television-575663462" rel="nofollow noopener"> on the part of</a> <a href="http://groupthink.jezebel.com/lets-talk-about-queer-baiting-on-television-575663462" rel="nofollow noopener">mainstream media</a>. But I have no interest in constructing some tricky tease in February and then disappointing a metric ton of readers in September. What would I possibly have to gain, except for an aggressive ulcer and possibly a gentle spattering of hate blogs? <i>The Raven King</i> is the last book in the cycle, and things are getting hairy, and there are a million things happening that I could tease; I have no reason to make something up to amuse myself or string readers along. <br><br>So when I say that I’ve <a href="http://maggie-stiefvater.tumblr.com/post/109356877296/mark-this-as-the-day-i-wrote-a-kiss-into-the-raven" rel="nofollow noopener">written two</a> <a href="http://maggie-stiefvater.tumblr.com/post/110871243396/mark-this-as-the-day-i-finally-wrote-that-other" rel="nofollow noopener">kisses</a> the fandom <a href="http://maggie-stiefvater.tumblr.com/post/110120803566/if-that-kiss-you-mentioned-writing-into-the" rel="nofollow noopener">was looking forward to</a>, I mean that they are genuine kisses, not ha-ha-it-was-all-a-dream or ha-ha-that’s-just-the-schnapps-talking or ha-ha-it-was-actually-Noah-kissing-a-potted-plant. <br><br>When I say that I’m going to kill Gansey, I mean I’m going to kill Gansey.<br><br>And when I say there’s something called the ORBMASTER in book four, I mean there’s something called the ORBMASTER in book four. <br><br>Did I say that last one before? Well. I’m saying it now.<br><br>Please rest assured in your dark heart that I am working up to something intentional and respectful. Please rest assured, also, that if I tease something that sounds dire, it’s gonna be dire. Please rest assured, thricely, that if I tease something that sounds great, it’s gonna be great. <br><br>Consider these my final remarks upon this subject until I drop the weighty block of <i>The Raven King</i> into bookstores this September.<br><br>urs,<br><br>Stiefvater<br><br><b>So, there we have it.</b><br><br>Update (1/4/15)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423016102i/13576748.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>i'm dead.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423016347i/13576778.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Here's a really well thought out theory:</b> (<a href="http://icarus.co.vu/post/102926766530/consider-this-gansey-is-glendower-more" rel="nofollow noopener">source</a>)<br><br>If you don't want to read through it all, here's the skinny. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Gansey is Glendower (the Raven King), Ronan is Iolo Goch (his poet), Blue is Gwenllian (his witch, his mirror), Adam is Artemus(?) (his magician) and Noah doesn't have an echo because he wasn't supposed to be there.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413507213i/11523010._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>. . . <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413507213ra/11523011.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> *nervous laughter* butbutbutbut it's Gansey!<br><br><b>If Gansey dies, I will die. <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413572638ra/11530511.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10568255705057504087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_924248391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/924248391" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/924248391?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2016">best-of-2016</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer924248391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15705427452691446263"><b>[Reread 3] Oct 2019</b><br/>For some reason this reread made me nearly cry??? Possibly because I still have about 3 weeks to wait until <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31373184.Call_Down_the_Hawk__Dreamer___1_' title='Call Down the Hawk (Dreamer, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Call Down the Hawk</a> and my heart officially aches so deeply for more time with dreamers and magicians. Possibly just because every time I reread this series, it fills another deep part of my heart. (I will absolutely be sentimental and teary right now, none can make me stopppp.)<br/><br/>This is a beautiful book. It unmakes you right before it fills you with wonder and whimsy and m</span>
  <span id="freeText15705427452691446263" style="display:none"><b>[Reread 3] Oct 2019</b><br />For some reason this reread made me nearly cry??? Possibly because I still have about 3 weeks to wait until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31373184.Call_Down_the_Hawk__Dreamer___1_" title="Call Down the Hawk (Dreamer, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Call Down the Hawk</a> and my heart officially aches so deeply for more time with dreamers and magicians. Possibly just because every time I reread this series, it fills another deep part of my heart. (I will absolutely be sentimental and teary right now, none can make me stopppp.)<br /><br />This is a beautiful book. It unmakes you right before it fills you with wonder and whimsy and magic.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>[Reread 2] Oct 2017:</b><br />So it's probably <i>a little bit obvious</i> that (a) this is my favourite favourite series, and (b) I still HAVE NO WORDS TO SUMMARISE WHAT IT MEANS TO ME. There are just some books/series that mean the absolute world to you because they fill you with everything you need. My heart is just <i>that full</i> whenever I read about the Raven boys. I love them. I live their story. I see MORE every time I read the books.<br /><br />Like just. HOLY FREAKING TREES. It was even better the second time and I may cry.<br /><br />• so originally I thought I didn't know what happened to Noah?? But this time, nope. IT EXPLAINS IT. I don't know how I missed it!<br />• I actually have realised there is an astronomically catastrophic level of Not Enough Pynch.<br />• where is my Ronan trilogy I need it now<br />• the level of FORESHADOWING AND CLEVER PLOT WEAVING slays me<br />• slayed lots of people hahhaha I'M SORRY IT'S TOO SOON<br />• it is so magical. it is pure magic<br />• it is complex and messy and beautiful<br />• I forgot that moment where Blue says "I want to be hanging out with my pretentious brat friends" and I'm like: same<br />• the ending makes me ache because I want more<br /><br /><b>Perfect book is perfect.</b> That's all there is.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW: April 2016</b><br /><br />OKAY SO I'M FINALLY <b>READY TO TALK ABOUT MY FEELINGS OF THIS MAGNIFICENT CREATURE OF A BOOK.</b> I have waited for this for <i>so so long</i>. omg. SO LONG. And I would like to take a hipster moment to also say <b>I've been a fan of Maggie Stiefvater for YEARS.</b> Which leads me to always feeling her books are so very personal to me. Like they just get into my heart and make a little house there and stab me frequently with pointy knives and yet <i>I still love them so so much</i>. <br /><br /><b>I loved this book.</b><br /><br />OBVIOUSLY.<br /><br />(And all spoilers will be hidden in spoiler tags. But if you don't wanna know anything -- DON'T READ, OBVIOUSLY.)<br /><br />...omg where do I even <i>start</i>?!??!<br /><br /><b>Firstly: the build up was so insane and my expectations were humungous.</b> Probably too high. I made too many theories and read too many tumblr posts and drooled over too much fanart and cried too man times in anticipation. <b>It didn't let me down, per se, NOPE. But it wasn't what I expected.</b> Which is fiiiiiine, to me, because I TRUST Maggie Stiefvater. <br /><br />I also knew a few things, from reading other Stiefvater books (like a MILLION TIMES) and I'm pleased that this is <b>still a very Stiefvatery book</b>. She must've been under SO MUCH PRESSURE for this one. But it was good. <b>It was right.</b><br /><br />ANYWAY. <b>
  <u>So let's compare my predictions/expectations to the realities:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>My predictions:</b><br />• Gansey would die and come back to life.<br />• Ronan might also die or at least <i>nearly</i> die, due to something Adam said in BLLB.<br />• That Gansey would come back as Glendower and possibly have to relearn what it is to be Gansey again with the help of Blue &amp; Co.<br />• The Grey Man and Maura would be AN ITEM FOREVER.<br />• Calla would make pie.<br />• #PYNCH WOULD SAIL.<br /><br /><b> The Realities Of These Predictions:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ • Gansey did die and did indeed come back to life. GO ME.<br />• Ronan nearly got unmade by the demon, but didn't seem THAT hurt. Still reflects on what Adam said in BLLB...ergo STILL GO ME.<br />• Gansey did not come back as Glendower.<br />• In fact, there was no Glendower. Biggest disappointment of my life.<br />• The Grey Man left possibly forever, possibly to return again when he'd killed bad people<br />• Calla made pie at least.<br />• PYNCH SAILED!!!!!!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>A LOT of my expectations were met! SO WHAT MORE CAN I ASK FOR?!?</b><br />Sure I was disappointed about a few things...but the characters were disappointed about a few things. And the fact that I felt what <i>the characters felt</i> can ONLY equal excellent writing, OKAY?!?<br /><br /><b>And omg there were so. many. plot. twists.</b><br />MASSIVE PLOT TWISTS. Some had me nearly shrieking my head off. Which was awkward since I was listening to an audio and my family thought I was INSANE (what's new, I suppose) but omgggg SO MANY EMOTIONS SO SO CONSTANTLY. <b>I was an entire ball of anxiety.</b><br /><br /><b>The shippy shipping was GOOD.</b><br />Maggie Stiefvater teased that there would be two kisses....*shrieks* THERE WERE TWO KISSES. PERFECT PERFECT PERFECT KISSES.<br /><br /><b>Also this book was downright freaking creepy.</b><br />Like the other books HAD been sorta creepy? But I don't know if this was just the audio...but this took the CREEP up a new level. I mean, we have a demon lurking around here now. But just the intensity of the darkness and how every sentence conveyed this leaking <i>demonic blackness</i> was just AMAZING. <b>I could feel it.</b> I was mildly terrified. Hahahha. Just, um, yeah, that's just the sound of my mind BREAKING..<br /><br /><b>DID I MENTION THAT I AM A BROKEN BEAN, YET?!?</b><br />BECAUSE I KINDA AM. IT WAS GOOD BUT THIS BOOK HURT OKAY????? I AM JUST AJFDKSLAFDJA I'M SO IN LOVE WITH IT AND JUST KIND OF A MESS OF bOOK HANGOVERS AND DREAMS AND BEAUTIFUL LYRICAL WRITING AND INTENSE CHARACTER LOVE.<br /><br /><b>All the characters changed and developed so so much.</b><br />And that's a huge reason I ADORE this series. The character development. They are REAL people and they all feel like my best friends. So I kinda feel like I'm <i>losing my best friends</i> now that this series is over.<br /><br />(Is it acceptable to reread yet? NO BUT REALLY...when my hardcover copy arrives, I'm re-reading immediately.)<br /><br />Okay, um, OH FORGET IT. I NEED TO TALK SPOILERS. ALL THE SPOILERS ---&gt; <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br /><b>OMGGGGG PYNCH.</b> Yes. That's what I want to talk about first. I knew it'd sail but I didn't know if it'd crash and burn? Because Ronan is a delicate <i>monster</i> and I was so scared he'd let his fear get in and he'd hurt Adam before Adam could hurt him. BUT IT WASN'T LIKE THAT. Ronan kissed Adam first. &lt;33333 And Adam returned it. AND ADAM LOVES HIM. And Gansey gave Adam the "okay so don't hurt my brother Ronan's heart" talk like the good big bro he is and that part melted me. I also 100% imagine that Adam goes off to college and returns in the holiday sand afterwards to be with Ronan at the barns. AND RONAN IS A FARMER AT THE BARNS. I think. I hope.<br /><br />Also that moment when <b>the demon was unmaking Ronan </b>and Adam was trapped in the back of the car and he couldn't <i>help or do anything to save Ronan</i>...that part got me. I. could. not. function.<br /><br />And I think the reason their ship is THE BEST is because <b>they both changed and grew SO MUCH.</b> They both had to learn to love. Ronan to love <i>again</i>. And Adam to love <i>in the first place</i>. AJFKDSJALKDJA JDK<br /><br />AND OF COURES <b>WE WILL TALK ABOUT BLUESY.</b> Who was wonderful. I think they peaked more in BLLB though, so Pynch stole ALL the scenes in TRK. They were so so adorable though and the kiss. The <i>kiss</i>. I wish it'd been described more kind of? Just when Gansey died <b>I felt it was nearly a bit rushed</b>. I expected him to stay dead for longer, for them to be more frantic about it. I expected more ENERGY around his death. But it was too calm. That saying, I'm not entirely complaining because a) MY HEART DIDN'T STOP WHICH WAS A REAL CONCERN, and b) maybe it was just the narrator of the audio book making it too slow/calm? I WILL FIND OUT WHEN I REREAD FOR MYSELF. <br /><br />I ship Blue and Gansey a LOT and I'm glad they're backpacking the world together. &lt;3 I hope they last though. I imagine Gansey will have to go off to college eventually and Blue too, but I hope that doesn't drive them apart. ;_; TRUE LOVE.<br /><br />Also I fully wanted Ronan and Adam to live together happily ever after at the barns and raise The Orphan Girl as their own. &lt;3333 YUP. Gonna keep imagining that headcannon.<br /><br /><b>As for the reveal of Glendower being always-dead?</b><br />I was disappointed. I was. But then SO WHERE THEY. So isn't that the point??? I am confused as to who the 3 sleepers were. If Gwenthlyin doesn't count because she didn't sleep? <b>So it was just Adam and the Demon...and....???</b> Was Blue the third sleeper since she found out she was a tree? (I'M FREAKING HAPPY WITH THAT BTW.) Or was Glendower actually there BUT they couldn't raise him because they didn't truly need him anymore? They'd grown past him, maybe?<br /><br />Also the fact that <b>Ronan made Cabeswater </b>was afjdkslajdslajfdk amazing. ADAM AND RONAN WERE MAJORLY CONNECTED FROM THE BEGINNING *SHRIEKS*<br /><br /><b>However I do have ONE massive confusion.</b><br />When Cabeswater was bringing Gansey back, it specifically said it couldn't make a human. So what did it make? How did it bring Gansey back? Is Gansey no longer human? I...I don't understand and I have many questions. 0_0 I wish that part had been explained better. <b>I wish there had been more about the epilogue.</b> I wish I knew what happened to Noah. No one even THOUGHT about him in the epilogue???? I LOVE NOAH AND I'M SAD BUT I LOVE HIM. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>SO OF COURSE I'M A RABID FAN OF THIS BOOK.</b><br />I love ALL Stiefvater books and this is no different. It's beautiful. It attacked my feels and got into my soul and totally CONSUMED my brain and I just <i>loved how it made me feel aaaaaall the things.</i> IT'S LEFT ME WANTING MORE. It's left me <b>believing in magic.</b> <br /><br />I AM SO VERY HAPPY.<br /><br />ALSO KINDA BROKEN.<br /><br />BUT HAPPY BROKEN.<br /><br /><br /><br /><i>(PS I would <i>love</i> to discuss it with you, of course, but please put any potential spoilers in spoiler tags. THANK YOU.)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15705427452691446263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1720551610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720551610" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720551610?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720551610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13287803033123273616"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He was a king. This was the year he was going to die.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I think a little piece of me died after I finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378527.The_Raven_King__The_Raven_Cycle___4_' title='The Raven King (The Raven Cycle, #4) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven King</a>. I am <b>numb</b> and <b>energetic</b>, <b>happy</b> and <b>sad</b>, <b>satisfied</b> and <b>insatiable</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470660358ra/19950061.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>And definitely <b><i>not</i> okay</b>.<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Richard Gansey III had forgotten how many times he had been told he was destined for greatness.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Depending on where you began the story, it was about <b>friendship</b>.<br/>Courage. Dedication. Loyalty.<br/>Magic.<br/>While Cabeswater kept fading, while Glendower remained hidden, Blue</span>
  <span id="freeText13287803033123273616" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He was a king. This was the year he was going to die.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I think a little piece of me died after I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378527.The_Raven_King__The_Raven_Cycle___4_" title="The Raven King (The Raven Cycle, #4) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a>. I am <b>numb</b> and <b>energetic</b>, <b>happy</b> and <b>sad</b>, <b>satisfied</b> and <b>insatiable</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470660358ra/19950061.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And definitely <b><i>not</i> okay</b>.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Richard Gansey III had forgotten how many times he had been told he was destined for greatness.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Depending on where you began the story, it was about <b>friendship</b>.<br>Courage. Dedication. Loyalty.<br>Magic.<br>While Cabeswater kept fading, while Glendower remained hidden, Blue and her raven boys had to make important decisions, untangle their feelings, understand the metaphysical powers that threaded their web around Henrietta and face demons and corruption and opportunists and monsters. The fight was difficult, sometimes hopeless, but they were never alone. They had each other, and that was enough. For how long though?<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What a strange constellation they all were.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I don't know what else to say about this series. I've already raved about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a>'s <b>poetic, soulful writing</b> and <b>subtle humour</b>, about the <b>enthralling plotline</b> and the <b>mystical ambience</b> and the <b>three dimensional characters</b> and the <b>all-consuming feelings</b> I've experienced thanks to them. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378527.The_Raven_King__The_Raven_Cycle___4_" title="The Raven King (The Raven Cycle, #4) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> was more <b>desperate</b> though. <b>Grim.</b> You could hear the clock ticking, you could sense the impending doom but could do nothing about it. Only relish Blue and her boys' presense, their fights and their bickerings and their unbreakable bond and wish that this bond would survive. That <i>they</i> would survive.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470663103ra/19950584.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He was a book, and he was holding his final pages, and he wanted to get to the end to find out how it went, and he didn't want it to be over.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>That's precisely how I felt. Forgive me for the dramatic note of this review, I just find goodbyes really, really hard. But even though I sobbed uncontrollably, even though my insides were ripped open and my heart bled, <b>I loved this book. Blue. Gansey. Noah. Adam. Ronan. Fearfully, awesomely, worshipfully.</b> The same way Ronan worshipped Adam, and Gansey worshipped Blue. Some questions remained unanswered. Some characters' fates unresolved. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What happened to the Gray Man? To Artemus? Gwenllian? Is Matthew alive? What was Persephone so desperate to find that she was killed in the process? How did Gansey salvage his relationship with his parents? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Yet somehow, I find it appropriate that a series thar started off with many secrets and questions finished the same way. Leaving you floating between reality and dreams. Not completely understanding everything but accepting it. It was a cycle. <b>A Raven Cycle.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Why do we breathe air? Because we love air? Because we don't want to suffocate. Why do we eat? Because we don't want to starve. How do I know I love her? Because I can sleep after I talk to her.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429076377ra/14526756.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But tears are liberating.<br>I feel blessed that I set off this <b>beautiful, heartwarming journey</b>. But now the time has come to say goodbye, and find a competent therapist.<br>See you on the other side.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13287803033123273616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_863716218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863716218" />
    <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source"><img alt="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586156113p2/6511257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/863716218?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source">Sue (Hollywood News Source)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer863716218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer566171936879110804">I vowed The Raven King would be the last Stiefvater's book I’m going to read. Even though that’s the case, I was genuinely optimistic for it. I want to wrap up The Raven Cycle in a satisfying note. I had fond memories of the characters, and I thought it’s only fitting.<br/><br/>However, the hopefulness ends right there.<br/><br/>Here’s some of the fundamental things I could tell you about this book:<br/> <br/>	 - If you hate the writing of this series, you probably won’t like it <i>still</i> <br/>	 - The swirling direction of the plot i</span>
  <span id="freeText566171936879110804" style="display:none">I vowed The Raven King would be the last Stiefvater's book I’m going to read. Even though that’s the case, I was genuinely optimistic for it. I want to wrap up The Raven Cycle in a satisfying note. I had fond memories of the characters, and I thought it’s only fitting.<br /><br />However, the hopefulness ends right there.<br /><br />Here’s some of the fundamental things I could tell you about this book:<br /> <br />	 - If you hate the writing of this series, you probably won’t like it <i>still</i> <br />	 - The swirling direction of the plot is confusing <br />	 - The author introduced a web of new plot, accompanied by new characters; it’s expected a lot of things are going to be sidelined, and forgotten <br />	 - It’s predictable. I anticipated the majority of the twist and concrete plan of the author <br /> <br />This is the every bit of part that made my skin crawl.<br /><br /><strong>This contains spoilers and text from the book.</strong><br /><br />The way Henry was introduced in BLLB was unforgettable. We saw him making an offhand rape comment. This is pretty common. See All For the Game series by Nora Sakavic where their <em>lone!good!moc</em> could be seen making the same proclamation throughout the series. I am willing to let it slide, maybe, this is not about race.<br /><br />In The Raven King, we get to know Henry Cheng better. He’s half Chinese and half Korean. His mother Seondeok is a Korean dealer of illegal antiquities. White authors can’t seem to write East Asians without associating them with mob, yakuza, and mafia? Another example: All For the Game series by Nora Sakavic<br /><br />This is the part where it gets nauseating.<br /><br /><em>“Principles? Henry Cheng’s principles are all about getting larger font in the school newsletter,” Ronan said. He did a vaguely offensive version of Henry’s voice: “Serif? Sans serif? More bold, less italics.”</em><br /><br /><em>Blue saw Adam both smirk and turn his face away in a hurry so that Gansey wouldn’t see, but it was too late.</em><br /><br /><em>“Et tu, Brute?” Gansey asked Adam. “Disappointing.”</em><br /><br /><em>“I didn’t say anything,” Adam replied.</em><br /><br />It was explicitly stated Henry’s second language is English. I’m going to assume Ronan is mocking the way Henry speaks, the intonation or accent of his voice. Whichever fucking way I look it is racist. Nobody even called Ronan out. The gross thing, the author made it into an “inside joke” for pynch.<br /><br />This didn’t end right there. We have another pynch scene where they made a punchline out of Henry’s ethnicity.<br /><br /><em>“Adam made puerile jokes at Henry’s expense (He’s half Chinese? “Which half?”) and sniggered clannishly; Blue called them on it (“Jealous, much?”): Gansey told them to put aside their preconceptions and think about him.</em><br /><br />Really? This made into the final publication? Minority’s ethnical identity isn’t a subject for crass puns.  Blue and Gansey’s meek intervention is not going to pacify me. I’m not here for this. Once again, this become a “cutesy” pynch scene.<br /><br />These vile ~scenes~ about Henry’s otherization serves no purpose. It doesn’t contribute anything to the plot. You can reason out the narrative is implying Adam and Ronan are jealous (of Gansey’s new attachment to Henry,) but the author could’ve made a different approach of executing that. This is deliberate.<br /><br />Another troubling scene with Henry and Blue<br /><br /><em>It was this: Blue, teetering on the edge of offence, saying, I don’t understand why you keep saying such awful things about Koreans. About yourself. And Henry saying. I will do it before anyone else can. It is the only way to not be angry all of the time.</em><br /><br />Great another Korean character written by white author who might or might not be experiencing internalized racism. Sounds familiar? See <a href="http://elloellenoh.tumblr.com/post/83411304305/whats-your-opinion-on-eleanor-park" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellen Oh’s intake of Eleanor and Park by Rainbow Rowell.</a><br /><br />I shipped pynch, but after this I’ll always associate them as that, “white gay couple who are lowkey racist.” The only comfort I have is I’m finally free of this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="566171936879110804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2288413104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2288413104" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2288413104?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=comments">comments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=i-love-these-characters">i-love-these-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=recommend">recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=magical-realist-urban-whatever">magical-realist-urban-whatever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2288413104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13213186925574903671">To whom it may concern,<br/><br/>This is not the last book of the Raven Cycle. It just isn’t. It’s not allowed to be. I didn’t say it was okay if it was and I feel like I should have some say in the matter, considering I like these books a lot and that’s pretty unusual for me. <br/><br/>Compelling argument, yeah? Everyone just send this review on over to Maggie Stiefvater and I’m sure we’ll have another installment in the next 12-18 months.<br/><br/>Great. Now that that’s settled:<br/><br/>WAS THIS MY FAVORITE BOOK OF THE RAVEN CYCLE?</span>
  <span id="freeText13213186925574903671" style="display:none">To whom it may concern,<br /><br />This is not the last book of the Raven Cycle. It just isn’t. It’s not allowed to be. I didn’t say it was okay if it was and I feel like I should have some say in the matter, considering I like these books a lot and that’s pretty unusual for me. <br /><br />Compelling argument, yeah? Everyone just send this review on over to Maggie Stiefvater and I’m sure we’ll have another installment in the next 12-18 months.<br /><br />Great. Now that that’s settled:<br /><br />WAS THIS MY FAVORITE BOOK OF THE RAVEN CYCLE???<br /><br />Probably not, right? It can’t be. Not when everyone warned me this book was going to be a touch disappointing and I five-starred Blue Lily, Lily Blue and put it on my all-time favorites list and screamed about it from the rooftops. It’s impossible.<br /><br />But also...this book was so damn good. I’m in crisis. Being in crisis is very normal for me, except usually I am in a negative crisis during which I manage to be somehow astonished that I disliked a book I was looking forward to, even though that’s basically my whole thing. <br /><br />Currently, I am in crisis because I loved a book so much it’s threatening to break my whole life. This is a YA FANTASY. I don’t love YA FANTASY. I’m not SIXTEEN YEAR OLD. I read YA fantasy and then I write eight-page reviews TEARING IT APART.<br /><br />Sporadic CAPS to make CLEAR that I am really FREAKING OUT ABOUT THIS. <br /><br />I’m going to do some categories and hopefully calm down. <br /><br /><br /><b>THE PLOT</b><br /><br />This whole book was very exciting.<br /><br />That’s really all I have to say. Feels like it shouldn’t be such an exceptional thing, but unfortunately it is. (The nonexceptional thing being “YA fantasy that is consistently exciting,” not “me not having a lot to say.” Although that too if we’re being totally honest.)<br /><br />Truly, why isn’t all YA fantasy exciting??? That should be #1 on the priority list. First and foremost, nonstop action; next up, love triangles or the not-like-other-girls trope or manic pixie dream girls or whatever other dumb sh*t authors are falling over themselves to include in their books.<br /><br />But I digress.<br /><br />This is SO FAST-PACED. For the most part, the other three books have a slow, kind of research-y feeling first half, where our characters are learning stuff and feeling angsty, and then an action-packed second half. THIS BOOK WAS BASICALLY ALL SECOND HALF. Which, stressful. But also awesome.<br /><br /><br /><b>THE SETTING</b><br /><br />I want the setting of this series to eat me, which is just about the highest praise for a fictional setting there is. <br /><br />I love being wrapped up in this world, and I would 10/10 be okay with living inside it. Not just because Gansey exists in it, but because it’s a world of magic and psychics and forests and sunlight and friendly ravens and dream-things and nature and accents and school uniforms and converted warehouses and miniature cities made of cardboard boxes and tucked-away mansions and perfect trees and talking trees and student housing and long drives and attics and also a pizza restaurant I really have an inexplicable soft spot for.<br /><br />These books are where 300 Fox Way is, and Cabeswater, and the Orphan Girl, and Chainsaw, and Monmouth Manufacturing.<br /><br />WHY AM I BEING FORCED TO STOP READING BOOKS THAT LET ME LIVE VICARIOUSLY AMONG THEM???<br /><br /><br /><b>SMALL COMPLAINTS BEFORE THE BEST STUFF</b><br /><br />I have exactly two (2) complaints about this near-perfect book, which is how you know my identity wasn’t stolen. Still the cynical, self-obsessed asshole who won’t let any of us have nice things.<br /><br />Having said that, here we go:<br /><br /><b>Complaint numéro un</b>: Piper, the greatest villain ever gifted to the genre of YA fantasy, or possibly any genre ever, is completely and utterly f*cked over in this book. She does not get even a fraction of the attention and love and villainous forehead-kisses she deserves. Which is a massive injustice. I may protest.<br /><br /><b>Complaint numéro deux</b>: Blue and Gansey are...so gross. <br /><br />I am very aware that saying this makes me look like a horrible freak monster who is somehow possessive over a fictional boy. That is not the case, and also I love Blue.<br /><br />Their relationship is just made up of 0% chemistry, 100% them doing gross stuff like staring at each other and rubbing faces and whatnot.<br /><br />No, I don’t have affection issues. Why do you ask?<br /><br /><br /><b>THE BEST STUFF (THE CHARACTERS)</b><br /><br />The title of this category looks like the weirdest remixed song title in all of history. But whatever. We have more important things to talk about. Namely:<br /><br />THIS IS PERHAPS THE FIRST YA BOOK EVER IN ALL TIME IN WHICH I HAVE LIKED EVERY CHARACTER.<br /><br />There wasn’t a single person I disliked. In the past I have made people very very mad at me due to the fact that someone could call either Ronan or Adam a congealing bowl of vanilla pudding to either of their respective fictional faces and I wouldn’t bat an eyelash. Which is to say I didn’t care about them that much. But in this book??? I, uh. I - I liked them both.<br /><br />FINE, EVERYONE. YOU WIN. I LIKED THEM AFTER ALL. But I didn’t like them when you said I would, so. Take your victory with a grain of salt.<br /><br />Adam/Ronan is the best and I am glad we’re getting more of them because that felt a touch: rushed. Which was maybe just me internally justifying the fact that suddenly I can’t get enough of RONAN??? AND ADAM??? Last-year me fresh out of Blue Lily, Lily Blue would never have been able to IMAGINE.<br /><br />There is not NEARLY enough of Noah, my small and spooky son, in this book. And that, alongside the dire lack of Piper, f*cking sucks.<br /><br />But there is also good news. Here is some good news:<br />- Blue is still completely rad<br />- Blue’s family of powerful women psychics = also still rad<br />- A boy named Henry Cheng appears, apparently for the sole purpose of bringing an even higher level of rad to the table<br />- And, of course:<br />- GANSEYGANSEYGANSEY.<br /><br />If you need to read me being disgusting about my love for a fictional character, please visit: literally any of my other The Raven Cycle reviews. I don’t have it in me right now. I am too devastated at my own loss. <br /><br />As this book says:<br /><br /><i>“Gansey.” A pause. “That’s all there is.”</i><br /><br />In conclusion: Please give me more Gansey. I need more Gansey.<br /><br />And everyone else is pretty cool too.<br /><br /><br /><b>FINAL EMOTIONAL RAMBLINGS, OR “THOUGHTS”</b><br /><br />Usually when I finish a series I really love, I feel an overwhelming sadness and slump forever and never ever want to read anything again except more books in that series and then they DON’T EXIST which cue sadness again. It’s a never-ending cycle of suffering.<br /><br />And don’t get me wrong, I am goddamn miserable that I finished these books. (The Gansey withdrawal alone is insufferable.) But this book actually managed to pull me <i>out</i> of my slump, not put me in one. <br /><br />Magic. <br /><br /><b>Bottom line</b>: I miss everyone already and I’m sad.<br /><br /><br />---------------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />I had tears in my eyes when I finished this book.<br /><br />TEARS. <br /><br />IN.<br /><br />MY.<br /><br />EYES.<br /><br />I'm furious and also I loved every second of it so stupid much. Review to come<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />I'M DOING IT.<br /><br />More than a year after finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2062288941?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a>, I'm finally attempting to finish this series.<br /><br />I HATE ENDINGS. <s>Pray for me.</s></span>
  <a data-text-id="13213186925574903671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1387294650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1387294650" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1387294650?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1387294650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7842617216180317143"><i>"The head is too wise. The heart is all fire."</i><br/><br/>There's two feelings currently fighting with each other: 1. Happiness 2. Disappointment. <i>The Raven King</i> was marvelous in so many ways, but unsatisfactory in the most important.<br/><br/>Maggie Stiefvater is a favourite author of mine because of reasons. Her stories are poetic and magnificent. Most of all, they live through their characters. Detailed and original, they are why I fell in love with the world around them. It's their realness that fascinates me, an</span>
  <span id="freeText7842617216180317143" style="display:none"><i>"The head is too wise. The heart is all fire."</i><br /><br />There's two feelings currently fighting with each other: 1. Happiness 2. Disappointment. <i>The Raven King</i> was marvelous in so many ways, but unsatisfactory in the most important.<br /><br />Maggie Stiefvater is a favourite author of mine because of reasons. Her stories are poetic and magnificent. Most of all, they live through their characters. Detailed and original, they are why I fell in love with the world around them. It's their realness that fascinates me, and their interaction that makes me happy. We have the Raven Boys, Blue, Blue's family and friends, the Grey Man, Piper, Gwenllian, Jesse Dittley, Orphan Girl, Kerah and Kavinsky. They are so alive. I'm a little in love with all of them.<br /><br />A few topics I'd like to adress:<br /><br /><b>Henry Cheng</b><br />A nice but unnecessary addition to an already complete and amazing cast. Throughout the novel I was uncertain if Henry was upfront or would turn out to be a backstabbing liar. I could have done without him and don't really understand his role in the first place.<br /><br /><b>Noah</b><br />Really, apart from being scary and dead, he didn't really do much in this book. I wished for more, if only for his sake. He deserved it.<br /><br /><b>Foretelling and Foreshadowing</b><br />This is what built up my expectations, what speeded up my heartbeat. There's nothing that creates curiosity, thrill and despair more than prophecies. Thanks for being so clever and cruel, Maggie.<br /><br />The one big issue I have with the book, is the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was anticlimatic and so...unremarkable. Glendower is plain dead. Only dust and bones. The discovery of Gwennlian was how it should have been. Magical and frightening, not ordinary and simple. No big favour granted. At least not in this way.<br />Let's not forget about the kiss. <b>The</b> Kiss. Anticipated for four books and more than a thousand pages and - exactly like Glendower - a let-down.<br />Here comes the confusing part: Cabeswater dies, Gansey comes back to life. But Cabeswater cannot really die. But still does. And Gansey doesn't. Cabeswater reshapes, makes itself human, dies, brings Gansey back to life, not quite human, but alive. And here Maggie loses me. I would've accepted this not-death, if Gansey's past-life (aka the epilouge) had told me how exactly not quite human he is. I'm afraid there was no such thing.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br />To say the least, there's too many loose ends. Too many, what-happeneds, too much uncertainty, too many unaswered questions. At least for my taste. (Please feel free to comment, discuss this book, and enlighten me.)<br /><br />However, the one big boost was Pynch. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Honest to god, this was nearly as good as that kissing scene in <i>A Gathering of Shadows</i>. My eyes had the shape of hearts, rainbows were coming out of my ears. And then, in the epilogue, Ronan was called Adam's <i>boyfriend</i>. Boyfriend. Boyfriend! I guess, I expressed my feelings well enough...but Boyfriend.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I take this end, this conclusion, and tell myself that it was about the journey and not the destination. And I think so much is true. Maggie Stiefvater gave me such a colorful set of characters and put them in a lovely and magical place. She put them into words, bound them between pages and hid them underneath such beautiful covers (no, really, just look at this beautiful cover!), only so I - so we - could live in this world and feel their feelings.<br /><br />It was an unbelivable journey, one that I will relive many, many times.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7842617216180317143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1809050680" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809050680" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1809050680?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407136646" href="/book/show/25394092-the-raven-king">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Petrik by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1809050680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13812043770968180905"><b>2.5/5 stars<br/><br/>This will be the last YA book I read for the year 2017.</b><br/><br/>The Raven King, the final book in The Raven Cycle series sadly doesn’t live up to the quality that the series had established. It is in my opinion that this is the weakest of the series, there are some great moments for sure but at the same time, there’s too many problems I had with it.<br/><br/><b>Picture: The Raven King by John Fenerov</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497375314i/23016976._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“He was a book, and he was holding his final pages, and he wanted to get to the end to find out how </blockquote></i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText13812043770968180905" style="display:none"><b>2.5/5 stars<br><br>This will be the last YA book I read for the year 2017.</b><br><br>The Raven King, the final book in The Raven Cycle series sadly doesn’t live up to the quality that the series had established. It is in my opinion that this is the weakest of the series, there are some great moments for sure but at the same time, there’s too many problems I had with it.<br><br><b>Picture: The Raven King by John Fenerov</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497375314i/23016976._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“He was a book, and he was holding his final pages, and he wanted to get to the end to find out how it went, and he didn't want it to be over.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Let me start off by saying that I love the complexity in the plot that the series offered. The overall main plot of the Raven King continues to captivate me endlessly and I was never bored with how the book starts and concluded. The last 100 pages of this book for instance were so hard to put down for me and I enjoyed the ending of the series. The strong bizarre atmosphere and the amount of danger looming for the characters in particular is one of my favorite part of the book.<br><br>The main characters development also remained top notch and with the exception for Noah, I love how each main character’s story concludes, especially Adam’s which I believe to be the best part of the book and maybe even the series. He came so far from where he began and he undergoes the most well written developments compared to the other characters.<br><br>And, Maggie’s prose again improved to be more engrossing and addictive to read. It’s the only reason why I never had any trouble reading this series or book despite how many problems I had with it.<br><br>Let’s start the part that didn’t work for me.<br><br>First, my number one main problem with the book, the entire middle sections of this book are mindlessly useless and out of the blue <i>(no pun intended)</i> to read. Here’s the thing, I will never agree with an author’s decision when they suddenly include a totally new character in the last entry of the series and have him/her be the new main character. Sadly, this particular problem can’t simply be overlooked in this book.<br><br>Once, I had a drinking contest with my friends 10 years ago, we all drank way too much and somehow, we all literally slept on the asphalt of a parking lot cause we thought it was too comfortable to let go. This is a true story and it became a good memory indeed. Oh sorry, the purpose of my story for this review? <b>Absolutely nothing, just like Henry Cheng’s purpose in the series.</b><br><br>Why in the world would Maggie thought it would be a good idea to have a completely new character appeared in the last book and have him included as the main character is something I will never understand. <b>Henry became Gansey’s instant best friend faster than my instant noodle being cooked.</b> It’s not that Henry himself is badly written or he’s a bad character, again, he’s not. It’s just that if you remove him from the story, it wouldn’t affect the story whatsoever and the fact that he had more spotlight than Noah, one of the main characters since the first book doesn’t really help the pacing of the book.<br><br>The worst part is, I’m pretty sure that Henry’s useless story itself took almost 200 pages in total. Seriously, I really think that Maggie included him for the sake of diversity only. Hey, let me tell you this, I’m Asian and I want him removed from the story. Gone baby gone please you damn RoboBee <i>(yes this is again, a new thing included in the last book).</i><br><br>Second, despite the main characters having a proper closure for their story, the amount of unresolved or unsatisfying conclusion to all the side character is insane. Almost all of them don’t have any proper closure; this includes the 300 Fox Way ladies that have been there since the beginning of the story. I won’t mention any of their names to avoid spoilers, all of them, that’s all I can say.<br><br>Finally, this may be me being nitpicky but there are three new characters here that were again, pointless and the way they were called annoyed the hell out of me. All three of them are literally called the same name, Lamouier <i>(or something I forgot their name already)</i>, I’m not kidding, the same name for all three of them. It really doesn’t help in understanding the narrative on which character is which. Is it so hard to put Lamouier 1, 2 and 3 in the narrative????<br><br>In the end, I don’t hate the series overall. The Raven Cycle is one of the most complex YA series I ever read <i>(heck the plot shouldn’t even be categorized as one imo)</i> and it have the characterizations that rivaled some adult fantasy books I read. However, rather than saying I hate this series or book, it’s more like I’m heavily disappointed by the last book because of the potential it had. Despite everything, I enjoyed my time reading this series and I didn’t regret it. The Raven Cycle however will be the last YA series I read for this year, there are countless other priority books that deserve my attention and the disappointment I had with this book doesn’t help in making me want to go back to this genre any time soon, not even as a break.<br><br><b>
  <u>Overall series review:</u>
</b><br><br>The Raven Boys: <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809050604?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">3/5 Stars</a>
</u><br><br>The Dream Thieves: <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809050647?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">3.5/5 Stars</a>
</u><br><br>Blue Lily, Lily Blue: <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809050662?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">4/5 Stars</a>
</u><br><br>The Raven King: <b>
  <u>2.5/5 Stars</u>
</b><br><br>The Raven Cycle series: <b>
  <u>13/20 Stars</u>
</b><br><br><i>This review is also featured on <a href="https://booksprens.wordpress.com/reviews/guests-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Booksprens</a><a></a> where I'll be a guest reviewer for this series, check it out! :)</i><br><br><i>You can find the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <a>BookNest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13812043770968180905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1584701759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer947951607619772095"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519888741i/25141739._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>1.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453987155?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven Boys</a> ★★★★★<br/>2.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1570709343?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dream Thieves</a> ★★★★★<br/>3.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577916432?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a> ★★★★★<br/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“He was a book, and he was holding his final pages, and he wanted to get to the end to find out how it went, and he didn't want it to be over.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/>This is truly a once in a lifetime series. If <i>Harry Potter</i> was my childhood, <i>The Raven Cycle</i> was my 20's. This series was perfect for me, and I don't think anyone could break the spell that this series and these characters have cast upon me. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“They were bot</blockquote></b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText947951607619772095" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519888741i/25141739._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453987155?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> ★★★★★<br>2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1570709343?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dream Thieves</a> ★★★★★<br>3.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577916432?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a> ★★★★★<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“He was a book, and he was holding his final pages, and he wanted to get to the end to find out how it went, and he didn't want it to be over.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>This is truly a once in a lifetime series. If <i>Harry Potter</i> was my childhood, <i>The Raven Cycle</i> was my 20's. This series was perfect for me, and I don't think anyone could break the spell that this series and these characters have cast upon me. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“They were both hungry animals, but Adam had been starving for far longer.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><i>“Depending on where you began the story, it was about..."</i> unconditional love and the power it can evoke. This book is the type of book that makes me want to be a better person. It makes me want to be more appreciative of my friends and family. It makes me so thankful that I have a love for reading and that it was instilled in me from a young age. It makes me feel so blessed that I'm able to read and able to read books like this. I'm eternally grateful to Maggie Stiefvater and her words that somehow penetrated my heart and built this perfect story.<br><br>I'm writing this review in actual tears, because this story is so beautiful and means so much to me. I probably sound really incoherent and this review is ending up just like my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80609960?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Shiver</a> review, where I'm just fangirling, but sometimes while reading this series I felt like Maggie Stiefvater was writing this solely for me. Like she somehow got inside my heart and wrote my soul down on paper. I really don't have any words that I can string together to do a review for <i>The Raven King</i> justice; I'll just say that it changed me forever, I'm eternally grateful to have had this reading experience, and that I'll never forget it. Thank you, Maggie Stiefvater.<br><br>Blue, Gansey, Adam, Ronan, and Noah all have a piece of my heart that I will never get back. In return, they will stay with me forever.<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“He closed his eyes and he began to dream.”</blockquote>
