<div id="review_1621094629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1621094629" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1621094629?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407136646" href="/book/show/25394092-the-raven-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1621094629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18003610623402442737">I'm buddy-reading this with... wait for it... you'll be so shocked when you find out (I've been working on my predictability)... my favorite exploding fluffball <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32524334-nina' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nina</a>, whose <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1570337074?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>review</a> you'd better read because WOW.<br/><br/><b>"His head was not thinking. His heart was thinking."</b><br/><br/>Would it be too mean of me to say "I told you"? Because <i>I did tell you</i> that this plot had neither rhyme nor reason. The first three books, plot-wise, were a huge disappointment, but the issue was overshadowed because of the great emphasis</span>
  <span id="freeText18003610623402442737" style="display:none">I'm buddy-reading this with... wait for it... you'll be so shocked when you find out (I've been working on my predictability)... my favorite exploding fluffball <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32524334-nina" rel="nofollow noopener">Nina</a>, whose <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1570337074?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> you'd better read because WOW.<br /><br /><b>"His head was not thinking. His heart was thinking."</b><br /><br />Would it be too mean of me to say "I told you"? Because <i>I did tell you</i> that this plot had neither rhyme nor reason. The first three books, plot-wise, were a huge disappointment, but the issue was overshadowed because of the great emphasis placed on the character development. (<i>And</i> even that had its flaws for me -I'm linking my reviews down below.) In order to cut the losses and save what could be saved,<b> the solution was an ending that tied up all the loose ends</b>, that made everything add up, that made every little piece fit in the bigger picture. And that, I think, would have been all the more effective here, with this series, which Stiefvater disseminated of so many <b>subtleties</b> and <b>nuances</b>. It could have been spectacular and magical, because Stiefvater's magic is in the <b> details</b> I mentioned before. And in <i>The Raven King</i>, she didn't play on it, and h**l if I know why.<br /><br />•I wrote way too many negative reviews lately, so let's start with the silver linings. Namely, Pynch. Holy, wonderful <b>Pynch</b>. (What a name for a ship, though.) I love how the complexity of <b>Ronan</b>'s character shows in this relationship. Reading his thoughts, you would never guess he's the same foul-mouthed boy of the crazy car races, the one with the shaved head and a tattoo on his back.<br /><br /><b>"The ocean burned."</b><br /><br />•<b>Adam</b>: now this may sound weird and unusual, but I've liked him since book one, and since book one he's always been my favorite character. I feel tears swelling up in my eyes if I think of his <b>growth</b>. He changed so much from the person he was in <i>The Raven Boys</i>, and his evolution follows a path that Stiefvater outlined with astonishing accuracy through all the four books. If for nothing else, I would recommend this series for Adam's sake alone: rarely have I seen such a <b>fleshed-out</b>, <b>round</b>, <b>deep</b> and <b>thought-provoking</b> character.<br /><br />•The <b>writing</b> is still one of the best things about this series. The first chapters were slighlty overstuffed with figures of speech, repetitions and parallelisms, and I think Stiefvater overdid a little, as if she wanted to make of the book a triumph in style, which grew old quickly enough. The rest of the book, however, is just as well-written as the rest of the series.<br /><br />And as the saying goes, the rest is meh.<br /><br />•<b>Cabeswater</b> and <b>chapter 67</b>.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, let me sum it up: Gansey is dead and the others think to bring him back to life sacrificing Cabeswater's life. Okay. But it turns out it's not that simple, and that Cabeswater can only "make some essential part of itself human-shaped". Brilliant (But I- Shut up!). And then: "It was impossible to bring him back changed [...] But it might be able to refashion him into something new". I could have lived with that so far. But then basically Cabeswater dies and Gansey is resurrected as good as new and <i>totally himself</i>.<br />Wait what? <br />Didn't you just say it was not possible?<br />Now, do we want to talk about how <b>cheap</b> and <b>nonsensical</b> this<b> I-kill-you-and-then-magically-and-haphazardly-resurrect-you</b> thing is? What was the problem? Too many fangirls' tears would have been shed if he'd truly died, probably. <br />What really bothers me about Gansey's non-death is the <b>poor excuse of an explanation</b> we were given. Cabeswater does things. Because of reasons. The End. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />•<b>Glendower</b>.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was the chase that Gansey needed; it was the quest, it was the journey, it was a lighthouse to head for. I get it, and I sincerely think it's a beautiful concept. But, to base four books on a quest that, at the end of the story, turns out to be <i>nothing</i>? At this point, does anyone care to explain me how Glendower fit in the whole thing? It only rekindles my impression that this series is made up of a bundle of loose threads absolutely unrelated and disconnected one from the other. <b>It kills the magic</b>. It mercilessly puts a dagger in its back and then stomps on its corpse.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />•<b>Blue's curse</b>.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ah, just joking. There is nothing to say about this. Only that we don't freaking even know if she and Gansey can now kiss or not. Fabulous. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br />I never liked her, by the way, and here she was just as insipid as ever. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And she's a tree. Like this, out of the blue (let's here it for me! Can you see how this book screwed with my mind or can you see how this book screwed with my mind?). Major lol. Can I laugh hysterically now? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />•<b>The boatload of secondary characters</b>.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This may sound impossible and hilarious (which it actually is), but we don't know a single thing about them. <b>Mr Gray</b> even was in a life-threatening situation and after that not a word about him is spared. <b>Gwenllian</b> is another open question, and Maura and Calla and Artemus. And Piper who says two lines and then dies? <br />And of course, then we have the <b>random new characters</b>: Piper's father(s ? They were three. Kind of), Seondeok, Orphan Girl, who was as cute as she was unnecessary.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />•<b>The fifth Raven Boy (or you know what, let's call him fourth) and the former fourth one.</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>Henry Cheng</b> is cute. Really. He's involved in this shameful case of <b>insta-friendship</b> and is thrown in the story so randomly that I don't know if I should laugh or cry, but okay, I'll deal with that. On the other hand, to balance his entrance, <b>Noah</b> practically disappears, as he gets barely two or three scenes in the book. I understand how awful this can be for his fans and how outraged they can feel now, but I can't help wondering why people are so surprised about this. It's not as if he had that much of a role in the previous books. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />•<b>Robo-bee and the dream things black market</b>.<br />The only word that comes to my mind, once again, is "<b>random</b>". None of this made sense, none of this had an actual purpose, none of this convincingly fit into the story. I waited until the end for some kind of stocktaking to bring some order in this mess, but I have still no idea of <i>why</i> what was happening was happening.<br /><br />➽ If you've read my other reviews (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1545926102?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1557986797?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dream Thieves</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1572181164?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a>) you probably remember I had <b>mixed feelings </b>about this series from the very beginning, and you also remember that my expectations for this book were extremely high. They were high because I saw how breathtaking the ending could be given how incredibly <b>promising </b>the base upon which to build it was. This story run toward a cliff with the intention to fly, but, in my eyes, all it did was plunge in the chasm. It felt <b>rushed</b>, hastily cobbled together, improvised. <b>I don't know what happened</b>. Everything was there, waiting only to be arranged a little.<br />It will take a while for me to process this wannabe conclusion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18003610623402442737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1058048742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3695590553924449382"><b>
  <i>“Stiefvater, please, I just want … ”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461662723i/18892618._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<b>That part? THAT PART? That part made me SO happy that it earn 10 stars. Yes. TEN.</b> <br/><br/>I already gushed and gushed and gushed about Ronan in my reviews for the previous books so I'm going to try and be more, well, to the point, let's say. If I can. Which is absolutely not sure at all, given that it's the last time I'll get to talk about him. <br/><br/>*GASP* <br/><br/>Okay, okay, I'm refraining my inner fangirl........ NOW. <br/><br/>ANYWAY. I always loved Ronan because for m</span></span>
  <span id="freeText3695590553924449382" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Stiefvater, please, I just want … ”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461662723i/18892618._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>That part? THAT PART? That part made me SO happy that it earn 10 stars. Yes. TEN.</b> <br><br>I already gushed and gushed and gushed about Ronan in my reviews for the previous books so I'm going to try and be more, well, to the point, let's say. If I can. Which is absolutely not sure at all, given that it's the last time I'll get to talk about him. <br><br>*GASP* <br><br>Okay, okay, I'm refraining my inner fangirl........ NOW. <br><br>ANYWAY. I always loved Ronan because for me he's the most complex character of them all : he's not someone whose personality can be grasped at once, fluctuating between anger and despair and intent and caring - God, so much caring, my heart can't take it. Ronan's a lost soul, trying to make sense of what his life became, trying to create a world at its own image - brilliant and mesmerizing and weird - the <i>best</i> kind of weird. His role of Greywaren stays one of the most wonderful thing I ever read about. <b>Ronan, so loyal to those he cares about, deserved every second of happiness he found here. I freaking adore him.</b> <br><br><b>My relationship with Adam... didn't follow the same path</b> : while my love for Ronan grew and grew and grew along the way, I'm not gonna lie, Adam's first impression wasn't good. AT ALL. Gosh, he annoyed me so much during my first read of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> - he was whiny, unfair, and his relationship with Blue just... didn't make me feel <i>anything</i>. <br><br>I wanted him to disappear, because I'm harsh like that when characters irritate me. <b>I am so glad he didn't.</b> <br><br>If Ronan stays my favorite, Adam's evolution is by far the most fascinating and <i>complete</i>. Granted, his relationship with Ronan - CAN I JUST SQUEAL TO EXPRESS MY GIDDY MOOD - has a lot to do with my acceptance of him, but it is not all. I always say that for me, the most difficult task for an author is to make me love a character I couldn't stand before. Trust me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a> owned it. I <i>lived</i> for his chapters in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378527.The_Raven_King__The_Raven_Cycle___4_" title="The Raven King (The Raven Cycle, #4) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> while they were like annoying bugs I wanted to crush in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> (sorry, bug). Give me an uncanny magician on any day. He's fantastic.<br><br><blockquote><b>"His feelings for Adam were an oil spill; he'd let them overflow and now there wasn't a damn place in the ocean that wouldn't catch fire if he dropped a match."</b></blockquote>
<br>Also, FUCKING FINALLY. I'm just sitting here and thinking about the best way to express my adoration for this ship, and honestly, I can't. These boys made me feel EVERYTHING, and they're simply too beautiful to be put into words (not mines, anyway - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a>'s work just great). Just know that I've got quotes to reread on many, many rainy days. <br><br><b>They offered me everything I wanted and then <i>more</i>. For that, I will cherish this book forever.</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461662723i/18892619._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>That part felt strangely remote and did not satisfy me. 2 stars.</b> <br><br>Don't get me wrong, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378527.The_Raven_King__The_Raven_Cycle___4_" title="The Raven King (The Raven Cycle, #4) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> gave me what I wanted - what I <i>needed</i> - with Adam and Ronan, and I would be lying if I said that the step back Blue and Gansey's relationship took had an impact on my reading experience. <br><br>It didn't. <br><br>Yet I could still feel the unfair treatment they were given, and for my friends who've been waiting for them, I feel obligated to acknowledge it. <b>Blue and Gansey did not give me any feels. Blue and Gansey were flat and boring.</b> Truth is, Ronan's always been my favorite, but never before did I want to SKIP Gansey's and Blue's chapters. Well, before this book anyway because here? Oh man, how did I want to sometimes. If I thought before that there was nothing more aggravating than reading about characters I didn't care about, I was wrong. <b>There's nothing more aggravating than reading about characters I <i>used</i> to care about and just don't anymore, not as much anyway.</b> I still like them as characters, but except for the very end, I felt as if I didn't know them, like all tension was erased as far as they were concerned. It's not that I wasn't satisfied with their fate, it's that I couldn't FEEL it. Thanks god their chapters were short. Ugh. Moving on. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461662723i/18892620._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>That part both pleased and disappointed me. 3 stars.</b><br><br>Look, I absolutely loved the way the story unfolded : the demon, Cabeswater (KERAH!) - <u>The plot was captivating and I loved every second of it</u>. <b>Except for <i>oh</i>, the loose ends everywhere.</b> <br><br>If <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378527.The_Raven_King__The_Raven_Cycle___4_" title="The Raven King (The Raven Cycle, #4) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> wasn't the ending of the series, I would probably rate it a 5 - or a strong 4.5. But the fact is, I cannot ignore that it <i>is</i> the ending.<br><br>What would have made for a perfect book <i>as part of a series</i> just cannot suffice for a <b>FINAL book</b>. The decayed wheel that Ronan finds in the epilogue is a perfect example of what I do not like to find in final books : the reference to future adventures to explain its presence feels like a cut-out, a lazy one at that. And do not get me started about Glendower because REALLY? It's all there is? Is there a joke I'm missing? (completely possible, considering that I read all night and that I'm not a wonder woman). <br><br><b>Am I the only one to wonder about...</b> <br>- Noah : I mean FOR CRYING OUT LOUD, what did she do with Noah here? <br>- MATTHEW : somehow, I still feel WORRIED for him even though I gathered that the Demon's death meant his survival. I would have wanted to actually SEE it, though.<br>- the Gray Man : what's up with him? Why am I feeling that he's only been used like a tool?<br>- Is Gwenllian staying at 300 Fox Way or what? Wandering around singing crazy songs? <br>- So, Glendower's quest was not the deal after all? Or was it? Or - ARGG. <br>- IS ARTEMUS LIVING IN A TREE FOREVER? Kidding, I couldn't care less about him. <br><br>I shall reread carefully this book and try to make sense of everything but for now, it feels like lacking. The ending felt so rushed and to be honest, I didn't expect that from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a> after all the foreshadowing I found during my reread of the three first books. <br><br><b>I needed more closure.</b><br><br>Also, another kiss for my beautiful boys but OKAY, I know we can't have it all. These boys though. They put such a happy smile on my face. SQUEEEE! (sorry sorry I know I said I wouldn't)<br><br>Here I am, trying to find a rating I would find appropriate for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378527.The_Raven_King__The_Raven_Cycle___4_" title="The Raven King (The Raven Cycle, #4) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a>, but the truth is, I can't. <b>This is a wonderful book that I enjoyed immensely with characters I will forever adore. Yet this is not a wonderful ending, BUT - </b> <br><br><b><u>FORGET EVERYTHING I JUST SAID. NO, REALLY. FORGET IT.</u></b><br><br><blockquote>"At the end of the Raven Cycle, I want readers … to <i>want</i>. <br>I don’t want them to be able to say what it is they want, though — I want it to be a bigger thing than words. I hope they get to the end and don’t know what to do for the rest of the day. I hope they feel unsettled and <i>needing</i> of <i>something more</i>. I want messages that say, “Stiefvater, please, I just want … ” and then silence. They don’t know what they want. They just <i>want</i>. <br><br>The Raven Cycle has always been a series about what makes a hero and about wanting something more, and while I can’t <i>expect</i> anything and be sure of it, that’s what I <i>hope</i> gets stuck in people’s minds."</blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Well done. I definitely do WANT. I can make a list, too.</b><br><br><b>PS.</b> <u>Please <b>spoiler tag your thoughts</b> in the comment section if needed</u>, I don't want my review to spoil anyone :) <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1439239610" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1439239610" />
    <a title="ily " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22496761-ily"><img alt="ily " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599357419p2/22496761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1439239610?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ily " class="user" itemprop="url" name="ily " href="/user/show/22496761-ily">ily </a>
      </span>

        rated it

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1134500133" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1134500133" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1134500133?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=yes-yes-yes">yes-yes-yes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134500133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13299961330434214807"><blockquote>
  <i>He was a book, and he was holding his final pages, and he wanted to get to the end to find out how it went, and he didn't want it to be over.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I am fairly certain there will never be anything quite like this series.<br/><br/>The story. The mystery. The magic. The characters. The romance. The <i>
  <b>friendship</b>
</i>. *clutches heart*<br/><br/>There are books I like. There are books I love. And then there’s <i>The Raven Cycle</i>. Words always escape me when I try to explain it, because I feel like no description can fathom how be</span>
  <span id="freeText13299961330434214807" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>He was a book, and he was holding his final pages, and he wanted to get to the end to find out how it went, and he didn't want it to be over.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I am fairly certain there will never be anything quite like this series.<br /><br />The story. The mystery. The magic. The characters. The romance. The <i>
  <b>friendship</b>
</i>. *clutches heart*<br /><br />There are books I like. There are books I love. And then there’s <i>The Raven Cycle</i>. Words always escape me when I try to explain it, because I feel like no description can fathom how beautiful and alive these books are.<br /><br />And when I say “alive,” I mean that everything about it feels so real to me. <b>The places.</b> I feel like I could step into anywhere in these books––300 Fox Way, Monmouth Manufacturing, the Barns, Cabeswater––and somehow I would know my way around (well … maybe not in Cabeswater, but you know what I mean). <b>The characters.</b> I literally feel like I <i>know</i> them. Each one is so unique, flawed, and lovable. And the relationships between them, whether they’re romantic or platonic, are so complex and beautiful.<br /><br />It’s all so incredibly vivid and enchanting. And I’ve really, truly never read anything like it. Honestly I think I can say that, in a way, <b>no story has ever felt so real to me</b>. If any book/series can make me believe in magic, it’s this one. <br /><br />Now, <i>The Raven King</i>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>He was a king. This was the year he was going to die.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Oh, how I dreaded this book. How I longed for it.<br /><br /><i>Blue Lily, Lily Blue</i> had ended on such a cruel cliffhanger, and I was desperate to know what would happen next. Then of course, the release date of <i>The Raven King</i> was delayed … what, three times? Every time I found out the date had been pushed back further, I died a little on the inside. It was unbearable. <br /><br />But at last, the day came! Unfortunately there was a delay of my shipment from Amazon, but I decided to just go ahead and buy the Kindle edition because <i>I could not wait one more day</i>. When I finally started to read it, it felt so surreal. Like, is this actually happening? Is this the real book and not a dream? I’d gotten so used to waiting and waiting for it, I could hardly believe it.<br /><br />As much as I wanted to make the book last, I just could not put it down. Sooo, I finished it within 24 hours. And just, wow. <i>Wow.</i> <b>This book was breathtaking</b>. It was emotional, terrifying, and just … gorgeous. Gorgeous, I say! <br /><br />When I first finished it, I wasn’t even sure what to think. But the more I’ve processed it and discussed it with friends, the more and more I love it. This book is important to me in so many ways, and I adore it for so many reasons. <br /><br />Ever since I finished it, I’ve been writing down all my thoughts/feelings about it in a document on my computer. It’s extremely long and rambling, and it took me a whole week to write it, but I’m going to try to fashion this into a (somewhat) coherent review. <br /><br />So, here we go.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>A WARNING: DON’T READ ANY FURTHER IF YOU DON’T WANT TO SEE SPOILERS. Sorry, but I feel like I can’t fully express my thoughts on this book without giving away … pretty much everything. So if you don’t want to be spoiled, do not read the rest of this review. This has been a PSA.</u>
</b><br /><br />—————<br /><br />Ahh, where to begin.<br /><br />First of all, <b>I think this was the scariest book of the series</b>––firstly because I was so scared for the characters, but also it had some of the most disturbing scenes/imagery:<br /><br />• Noah getting possessed by the demon and trying to gauge Blue’s eyes out<br /><br />• Adam getting possessed by the demon and not being able to control his eyes/hands (and trying to kill Ronan––nooooo!)<br /><br />• Ronan almost getting “unmade”<br /><br />• Geez there was a really high body count in this book: Aurora, Neeve, Greenmantle, Piper, Gansey (sort of??). And they all died in such awful ways (well except Gansey, if we’re counting him). <br /><br />• Just … the demon. *shudders* And Cabeswater getting so corrupted. <br /><br />There were so many haunting parts that I will not soon forget.<br /><br />But what’s even more unforgettable is <b>the friendship</b>. *throws sparkles* … Okay, but really, I love the friendships in this series <i>so much</i>. They’re all so dedicated to each other, and it fills my heart with rainbows. <br /><br /><b>And a special shout-out to Ronan and Blue––oh my gosh, these two are the BEST BROS.</b><br /><br />Exhibit A:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“… I got suspended,” Blue replied.<br /><br />“Get the fuck out,” Ronan said, but with admiration. “Sargent, you asshole.”<br /><br />Blue reluctantly allowed him to bump fists with her as Gansey eyed her meaningfully in the rearview mirror.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Exhibit B:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>”Look, Sargent,” Ronan retorted. “I was gonna dream you some eye cream last night since clearly modern medicine’s doing jack shit for you, but I nearly had my ass handed to me by a death snake from the fourth circle of dream hell, so you’re welcome.”<br /><br />Blue looked appropriately touched. “Ah, thanks, man.”<br /><br />“No problem, bro.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />And can we just stop for a second and talk about how <b>the world was like literally ending, and Ronan went out of his way to find <i>magical eye cream for Blue’s injured eye</i>??</b> Seriously, Ronan Lynch is too good for this world, too pure. (Not to mention, at the beginning of the book he was also still trying to find some kind of cure/protection for Gansey. *ugly sobbing*)<br /><br /><b>I also really love the friendship between Blue and Noah.</b> I’ve always loved the friendship between these two, and in this book it was particularly bittersweet. <br /><br /><blockquote><i>Blue didn’t care that he––it––Noah––was strange and decaying and frightening. She knew that he––it––Noah––was strange and decayed and frightened, and she knew that she loved him anyway. <br /><br />She hugged it. Him. Noah. She didn’t care if he wasn’t quite human anymore. She would keep calling whatever this was </i>Noah<i> for as long as it wanted to be called Noah. And she was glad that he could read her thoughts in that moment, because she wanted him to know how thoroughly she believed that.</i></blockquote><br /><br />EXCUSE ME WHILE I UGLY-CRY IN THE CORNER.<br /><br />Oh and speaking of ugly-crying …<br /><br /><b>THE ROMANCE</b><br /><br />Brace yourselves for some next-level fangirling. I’m sorry, so sorry. <s>I’m not, though.</s><br /><br />Well, let’s start with <b>Blue and Gansey</b>:<br /><br />They are just so cute together. (I especially loved the toga party scene!!) And I was glad they finally told everyone about their relationship––even though it was already super obvious, but whatever. (I also liked when they held hands and Ronan just said “Gross.” Just … omg, Ronan.) <br /><br />And ah yes the kiss, that deadly kiss. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>He had dreamt of it often enough, and here it was, willed into life. In another world, it would just be this: a girl softly pressing her lips to a boy’s. But in this one, Gansey felt the effects of it at once. Blue, a mirror, an amplifier, a strange half-tree soul with ley line magic running through her. And Gansey, restored once by the ley line’s power, given a ley line heart, another kind of mirror. And when they were pointed at each other, the weaker one gave.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />*SOBBING* DON’T TOUCH ME.<br /><br />Okay but honestly, wow what a sadly beautiful passage. Four whole books led up to this moment, and it was so wonderfully written. I just literally couldn’t breathe <s>and neither could Gansey, am I right?</s><br /><br />Also I’m glad that these two ultimately got a happy ending, because I wasn’t so sure that was going to happen. <br /><br />Nowwww moving on to …<br /><br /><b>RONAN AND ADAM. RONAN AND ADAM. OH MY GODDDDDDD.</b><br /><br />*Ah-hem* Okay, REALLY brace yourselves for this, because I have a hell of a lot to say. And I’m not sure how to put all my emotions into words, so here are just some of my absolute favorite Pynch moments:<br /><br />• Adam making Ronan’s shitty music play in Cabeswater just to make Ronan laugh.<br /><br />• <i>
  <b>Adam smiled cheerily. Ronan would start wars and burn cities for that true smile, elastic and amiable.</b>
</i> MY HEART. <br /><br />• THE KISSES. OH MY, THE KISSES. When Ronan kissed Adam, I had to like … stop for a second because I was like “OH MY GOD, THIS IS REALLY HAPPENING.” And uggh just what a beautiful scene in every way. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Once, when Adam had still lived in the trailer park, he had been pushing the lawn mower around the scraggly see yard when he realized that it was raining a mile away. … He had plenty of time to put the mower away and get under cover. Instead, though, he just stood there and watched it approach. Even at the last minute, as he heard the rain pounding the grass flat, he just stood there. He closed his eyes and let the storm soak him.<br /><br />That was this kiss.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />HOLY. SHIT.<br /><br />Okay, but what’s even more beautiful than that first kiss is the second kiss:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>When Adam kissed him, it was every mile per hour Ronan had ever gone over the speed limit. It was every window-down, goose-bumps-on-skin, teeth-chattering-cold night drive. It was Adam’s ribs under Ronan’s hands and Adam’s mouth on his mouth, again and again and again. It was stubble on lips and Ronan having to stop, to get his breath, to restart his heart. They were both hungry animals, but Adam had been starving for longer.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />OH MY GOD you should’ve seen my dumb face when I was reading this part. Literally I had to keep my hand over my mouth because <b>I was smiling so hard I felt like my smile might fly off my face or something</b>. I had goddam tears in my eyes. UGGGGH. <br /><br />I just … *takes a deep breath* Oh man. I’ve been shipping these two since the second book, but I wasn’t sure it would actually happen. But it did, it did, and I haven’t stopped smiling about it for a whole week now. AAAH.<br /><br />But wait, there’s more!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>When he opened his eyes, he saw that Ronan was looking at him, as he had been looking at him for months. Adam looked back, as he had been looking back for months.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />*HEART EYES* <br /><br />• Gansey finding out and just telling Adam not to hurt Ronan like the protective Mom Friend™ that he is.<br /><br />• Chainsaw sitting on Adam’s shoulder!!!!!!!<br /><br />• The part where Adam is possessed and tries to kill Ronan, and <b>Ronan is literally more willing to let Adam kill him than to hurt Adam in defense:</b> “<i>The choice was death or hurting Adam, which wasn’t much of a choice at all.</i>” I’M NOT CRYING, I JUST … HAVE A BRICK IN MY EYE. *cries* <br /><br />• Adam driving Ronan’s car and listening to Ronan’s music. Adam’s shitty dad mockingly being like “I see you’re driving your boyfriend’s car!!” and <i>Adam not denying it</i>. <br /><br />• Ronan and Adam adopting a small goat child???? Omfg they are actual dads<br /><br />All right, I could go on and on but I will shut up now. Basically, I AM SO HAPPY FOR THESE PRECIOUS CHILDREN (can you tell?). They’ve been through so much and they deserve it, holy shit. It just fills me with joy to see these two so happy and in love. UGH. <br /><br />Plus, A) there’s no bullshit Tragic Gay Ending™ (THANK YOU JESUS), and B) Adam is a canon bisexual and honestly that means so much to me. And just in general, these two mean so much to me. *collapses*<br /><br />• Oh and one last thing about the romance in this book/series in general: I like that within the romances, there’s so much focus on friendship. That is, part of why I love these pairings is that they care about each other as friends as well as in a romantic way. For example:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>[Blue] just wanted to keep being best friends with Gansey forever, and maybe one day also have carnal knowledge of him.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I mean, obviously that’s meant to be funny––but I think it’s also an important mentality that I feel is uncommon: that is, that friendship is a part of romance and they’re not mutually exclusive?? I’m not sure how to put it into words, but hopefully I’m making sense.<br /><br />Well anyway, some other things I wanted to talk about …<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Glendower</u>
</b><br /><br />First of all, I thought it was fitting that Glendower was buried under the mansion where Gansey died (and came back to life). So ~symbolic~ but also not what I expected.<br /><br />And … Glendower was dead the whole time. Wow. Also not what I expected, and yet it weirdly made sense. I feel like all the characters had to find something in themselves to stop the demon, and it would’ve been a huge cop-out if Glendower had just killed the demon and saved Gansey.<br /><br />In a way it was anti-climatic, but it was in a good way?? That is, I expected when they found Glendower it would be like, magical rays of light shooting out everywhere, and some great bit powerful being rising up from the grave or whatever. But when he was just a dead body it felt … right, somehow. Like, oh. They actually didn’t need him all along.<br /><br />It was really sad how Gansey broke down crying afterwards. I hated to see him so crushed and heartbroken. But, I also think he needed to see that Glendower was dead. <i>He needed to see that he could still be himself without Glendower</i>, and that he’s capable of facing his fears by himself. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Ronan dreamt Cabeswater</u>
</b><br /><br />WHAT. Another thing that I did not see coming. Yet when I found out I was like, “… Oh, that makes sense.” Which is basically exactly what Gansey thinks:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>… Gansey was slightly confused. He felt as if he was being told a secret that he’d already been told before. He couldn’t tell if this was because Cabeswater itself had possibly already whispered this truth to them on one of their walks there, or if it was merely that the weight of evidence was already so conclusive that his subconscious had accepted ownership of the secret before the parcel had been officially delivered.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Haha yup, that about sums it up.<br /><br />But also the more I think about it, there were SO many signs that pointed to this. And also it gives me a lot of feelings. Because like, as I’ve seen some people point out, Cabeswater:<br /><br />- is bound to Adam<br />- will do whatever Gansey asks it to<br />- and is really nice to Blue<br /><br />So basically Cabeswater IS Ronan and I’m crying again<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Blue is a tree … person?????</u>
</b><br /><br />Well … also not a twist I saw coming, and I’m still not entirely sure what to think of it. Obviously I always knew there was something special about Blue, this just wasn’t what I thought it would be. I’ll have to go back and re-read the other books eventually, but I’ve seen some people say that there was foreshadowing to this in the earlier books, so … *shrugs* Also I think it’s kind of hilarious. <br /><br />The one thing I don’t get is how Blue can like telepathically communicate with Gansey with her magic tree powers?? I don’t really understand. But, okay. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Gansey’s death/rebirth<u></u></u>
</b><br /><br />I mentally prepared myself for this terrible moment for months and months, and I still did not feel ready for it. Surprisingly, I didn’t cry when it happened. I just felt kind of numb. But also like, “Lol okay so he’s going to come back to life, right? RIGHT???”<br /><br />And ugh Ronan’s reaction killed me the most:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Ronan crouched beside him, black still smeared on his face under his nose and around his ears. His dreamt firefly rested on Gansey’s heart. “Wake up, you bastard,” he said. “You fucker. I can’t believe that you would …” <br /><br />And he began to cry.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />JUST RIP MY GODDAM HEART OUT.<br /><br />I also liked that it turned out the voice Gansey heard was Noah’s and not Glendower’s. Whoa. <br /><br />But anyway.<br /><br />As for Gansey coming back to life: well, I have somewhat conflicted feelings. I always knew that I was going to be mildly pissed off about whatever the outcome was. So part of me is like “that’s kinda lame” since you know, the whole series kind of revolved around him dying at the end. But then again, I really like that they all had to craft a new Gansey out of Cabeswater/themselves––because symbolically, that’s really nice, how he ends up being made up of pieces of all of his friends. And I feel like that’s what the book/series is really about. And also Gansey gets to live, so YAY! <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Just … the ending in general</u>
</b><br /><br />The more I think about it, the more I love the ending. At first I was kind of like, “That’s it?” but I think that was just the shock of it being over forever. Now that I’ve had time to process it, it all feels right. It’s fittingly bittersweet. While it’s happy in some aspects, it’s not perfect. Blue meets her father and learns who he is, but he’s incredibly distant. They find Glendower, but he’s dead. Gansey comes back to life, but he’s not exactly the same person. Noah doesn’t get to stay forever. Adam confronts his parents but he doesn’t really forgive them. It wouldn’t have felt as believable if everything had been tied up in a neat bow, so I’m glad that not everything was perfect in the end. And yet, it was still very hopeful. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Some closing miscellaneous thoughts:</u>
</b><br /><br />• Really my only big criticism is that <b>I wish there’d been more Noah</b>, or at least that he’d gotten more acknowledgment. I understand he was fading away and whatnot, I just wish there’d been a little more closure with him and the other characters. I liked that one really sweet scene between him and Blue, but otherwise I felt like at the end they were all like, “Noah who??” At the very least I wish we’d gotten to see how everyone felt about him being gone, but oh well.<br />• <b>I liked Henry Cheng.</b> For some reason I spent the whole book thinking he would turn out to be evil or something and I really hoped he wouldn’t, but he didn’t. So. I’m glad about that. He was pretty cool.<br />• Okay don’t ask me why, but for some reason <b>I really thought Chainsaw was going to die??? So I’m happy she didn’t! :)</b><br />• <b>I’m also happy Ronan and Declan made up.</b> It was really sweet. <br /><br /><b>The final word:</b><br /><br />I LOVE THIS BOOK. I LOVE THIS SERIES. <br /><br />Thank you, Maggie Stiefvater. I don’t know what else to say.<br /><br /><i>That’s all there is.</i> ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13299961330434214807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1948964733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17775232083469476095"><b> 4.5 Stars <br/><br/>Overview: Re-Read </b><br/><br/>This time around I enjoyed Gansey and Blue's stories more? Their development is more subtle than Adam and Ronan's, but it is there.<br/><br/>This leaves a LOT of questions? There's a character in mortal danger, the chapter ends in a cliffhanger and then The Big Thing ™ happens somewhere else and we NEVER go back to see what happened to that character? I'm assuming it's all good?<br/><br/>^Stuff like that is the only reason this isn't 5 stars. Still has some amazing, beautiful scenes tha</span>
  <span id="freeText17775232083469476095" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 Stars <br /><br />Overview: Re-Read </b><br /><br />This time around I enjoyed Gansey and Blue's stories more? Their development is more subtle than Adam and Ronan's, but it is there.<br /><br />This leaves a LOT of questions? There's a character in mortal danger, the chapter ends in a cliffhanger and then The Big Thing ™ happens somewhere else and we NEVER go back to see what happened to that character? I'm assuming it's all good?<br /><br />^Stuff like that is the only reason this isn't 5 stars. Still has some amazing, beautiful scenes that are my favorite in the series. JUST STILL SO MANY QUESTIONS <br /><br />(AND WHY IS HENRY STILL THIRD-WHEELING?)<br /><br />---------------------<br /><br /><b>First Read:<br /><br />4 Stars </b> <br /><br />Ugh. What am I supposed to do with my life now?????<br /><br />This is really hard to rate, because parts of it were <i>fantastic</i>. Some of the characters and plots achieve perfect closure and their development was everything I hoped for and more.<br /><br />But some things still feel really unresolved? And it feels like some character storylines are oddly unfinished?<br /><br /><b>Adam</b><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Need was Adam’s baseline, his resting pulse. Love was a privilege. Adam was privileged; he did not want to give it up. He wanted to remember again and again how it felt.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />-	It’s a well-established fact he’s my favorite, but in case you couldn’t tell—HE’S MY FAVORITE AND I LOVE HIM A LOT.<br /><br />-	Has a perfect, well-developed character-arc with <i>fantastic</i> resolution.<br /><br />-	Seriously. I’m not just saying it because he’s my favorite (which he is) or because I love him a lot (which I do) but because it's actually exceptionally well done. Adam’s development can be easily traced throughout the series.<br /><br />- It's most easily trackable in his relationship with his family and sense of self-worth. He’s still an incredibly flawed, well-rounded character, and it was great seeing him discover his agency.<br /><br /><b>Ronan</b><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Dreamers are to be classified as weapons. <br />Ronan already knew he was a weapon ; but he was trying to make up for it.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />-	Broke.me.<br /><br />-	Seriously. When Ronan cries, <i>I cry.</i><br /><br />-	I still ship it so hard omfg. <br /><br />-	His overall development was so gradual and perfectly timed. And it really cultivates into this really beautiful story and character.<br /><br />-	Ronan’s relationship with Cabeswater is <i>awesome.</i><br /><br /><b>Blue</b><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I don't care to be pretty," Blue shot back hotly, "I care to look on the outside like I look on the inside.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />-	There wasn’t really any development? She’s still kinda the same Blue she was in the first book? Which I guess isn’t a <i>bad</i> thing. It just feels kinda redundant.<br /><br />-	I honestly couldn’t care less about Blue’s heritage. It didn’t impact the plot or really tell me anything I didn't know... and it all felt really rushed? <br /><br />-	I will say I like how her character ends up. She’s always had this sort of wanderlust and I think her ‘end’ destination reflects that. It also makes previous conversations more poignant and meaningful. But it still didn’t feel like <i>enough?</i> <br /><br /><b>Gansey</b><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Richard Gansey III had forgotten how many times he had been told he was destined for greatness.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />-	…Is that all?<br /><br />-	His ‘big moment’ felt rushed. What there was of it was very beautiful, but the aftermath was almost nonexistent.<br /><br />-	In fact I just feel kind of let down by his arc overall. There was a lot of talk of greatness and a <i>ton</i> of build-up, and it just felt underwhelming? <br /><br />- Still just want to grab a beer with him, tbh<br /><br /><b>Noah </b><br /><i>
  <blockquote> 'Don't throw it away.' </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />-	I don’t actually have a lot to say about Noah, but there's focus on him as a character instead of a plot device (though there's certainly plot) and I felt like he finally deserved his own thing.<br /><br />-	His ending was super abrupt and <i>never</i> talked about.<br /><br /><b>Others</b><br /><br />-	No resolution for any of the women at Fox Way. I guess once they stop being useful, we're just supposed to forget them?<br /><br />-	No resolution for The Gray man. I mean, maybe? Kinda? But I’m still not really sure what happened to him.<br /><br />-	It’s not that I <i>hated</i> Henry. It’s just that he was completely irrelevant and I’m not sure why he existed at all. <s>(actually I might have hated him a little)</s><br /><br />-	This made me feel for Declan when I thought I hated him. All these Lynch brothers are so much more than their first impressions.<br /><br />-	What the frick even happens to Gwenlillian and Artemus?<br /><br />-	Okay so nobody throw things at me, but I don’t see the point in Orphan Girl? Why does she exist? Why is she here? Is she even supposed to mean anything? It just all felt so <i>random</i> and didn’t really impact the overall plot. <br /><br /><b>In Conclusion: </b><br /><br />Looking back on this, it seems like I listed a lot of negative and it doesn't feel like an accurate representation of this series. So I just want to clarify, while this was my least favorite of the series, the series itself is <i>crazy good.</i><br /><br />This book had several great parts, and the parts I enjoyed were <i>exceptional</i>. Almost completely makes up for the rest and I wish I could rate this higher.</span>

<div id="review_1146029997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1146029997" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1146029997?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=most-anticipated">most-anticipated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=best-reads-of-2016">best-reads-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=published-2016">published-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1146029997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13417793469173554151">As I’m writing this, I am actually physically trembling. I don’t think I’ve ever been this emotional about any book ever (not even the last Harry Potter book). That is how much I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378527.The_Raven_King__The_Raven_Cycle___4_' title='The Raven King (The Raven Cycle, #4) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven King</a>.<br/><blockquote>"At the end of the Raven Cycle, I want readers … to <i>want</i>. I don’t want them to be able to say what it is they want, though — I want it to be a bigger thing than words. I hope they get to the end and don’t know what to do for the rest of the day. I hope they feel unsettled and <i>needing</i> of <i>something mo</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13417793469173554151" style="display:none">As I’m writing this, I am actually physically trembling. I don’t think I’ve ever been this emotional about any book ever (not even the last Harry Potter book). That is how much I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378527.The_Raven_King__The_Raven_Cycle___4_" title="The Raven King (The Raven Cycle, #4) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a>.<br /><blockquote>"At the end of the Raven Cycle, I want readers … to <i>want</i>. I don’t want them to be able to say what it is they want, though — I want it to be a bigger thing than words. I hope they get to the end and don’t know what to do for the rest of the day. I hope they feel unsettled and <i>needing</i> of <i>something more</i>. I want messages that say, “Stiefvater, please, I just want … ” and then silence. They don’t know what they want. They just <i>want</i>.</blockquote><br />Really, it can no longer be surprising that Maggie Stiefvater, the queen of words, would be better able to describe my feelings about the Raven Cycle than I can. Because this description is literally me right now. I cannot even try to express my feelings on this book or the series as a whole. Where would I start? What would I say? What if I say something wrong because I missed a detail or interpreted a message differently? <b>I know I’m a reviewer and I love writing reviews so much but sometimes words fail me. This is one of those times.</b><br /><br />This is not a review. It is a gathering of different thoughts, a Pinterest board of random contents of my brain, a playlist of feelings. If you do not want to read my inner ramblings, I completely understand. Just know this: <b>The Raven Cycle is exceptional. It’s beautiful and thoughtful and will give you SO MANY FEELINGS.</b> Admittedly, it is not a series for everyone. If you’re a reader who reads for the thrill of a fast-paced plot with twists around every corner and have trouble enjoying books that are more meandering and character driven, maybe this series isn’t the best choice. <b>But if you read to fall in love with characters, to experience wonder, to flip to the last page and have the story continue in your mind, then this is exactly what you’re looking for.</b> <br /><br />I read <i>The Raven Boys</i> when it was first published in 2012. That was way before I started writing reviews, before I discovered Goodreads. Having finished it now I can officially say that it is <b>my number one favourite series</b>. That’s extreme, I know, but there just hasn’t been another that could evoke in me the same emotional response. These books aren’t just stories; they are literary masterpieces. <b>And they are personal to me in a way that I don’t feel about any other book.</b> I know that with every reread I will discover something new, that pieces will click into place I didn’t even know were askew. The messages and characters will stay with me for a very long time, perhaps forever.<br /><br />In short: <b>I love these characters and their never-ending complexity, I love Maggie’s writing style that is simultaneously odd and familiar (also, her freaking dialogues are ON POINT), I love the setting that came to life in my mind, I love the intricacy of the plot with its foreshadowing and miniscule pieces falling into place, I love the character development that is some of the best I’ve ever seen, I love that this series is so unique and not afraid to be different. Oh, and it goes without saying that: ULTIMATE SQUADGOALS.</b><br /><br />The Raven King contains many of my favourite scenes of both the series and all books in general (these are just a few):<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <br />- The scene with Ronan and Adam in Ronan’s bedroom. I couldn’t breathe.<br />- Blue and the women of 300 Fox Way when they’re asking Blue what she wants to do with her future (sitting in the bathtub). One of the most heartfelt things I’ve ever read.<br />- Ronan and Declan on the roof. This is what true family looks like.<br />- The hilarity that was the scene when Blue is waiting for her school bus. Because Maggie knows exactly what her characters’ flaws are and has no problem showing it. And because WE ARE ALL HYPOCRITES IN ONE WAY OR ANOTHER. <br />- When all of them are at the hospital and Gansey finally tells Adam about him and Blue, and Ronan, that sweet little cinnamon roll, says all the right things at the right time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I feel like going into more detail would just end nowhere, so instead I’ve decided to address some of the issues my GR friends (who are all phenomenal reviewers) had with the series. Just a disclaimer: this is by NO MEANS a criticism of them. Every issue they brought up is 100% justified.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><b><u>Not enough Noah</u></b><br />Yes, I get it, I love Noah too, and I wish we would have seen more of him in this book. Having said that, the lack of Noah wasn’t an issue for me, especially with how the series ended. For me, <b>Noah was a symbol</b>. A symbol for new beginnings and letting go of the past. Our characters are growing up and moving away from Henrietta, and Noah cannot leave with them. He’s dead. Ultimately, the gang has to let go of him, the way we all need to let go of things when we grow up. Also, in the end, he played such an important part in the book. I mean, he is the reason Gansey is still alive! His death is what saved Gansey twice! (At least that was my interpretation.) <br /><br /><b><u>Why on earth is Henry Cheng so important? He’s a new character!</u></b><br />Admittedly, this didn’t strike me as that weird because I read Maggie Stiefvater’s recap of <i>Blue Lily, Lily Blue</i> on Recaptains, and so I knew Henry would be important (if you read the recap you know what I’m talking about). For me, his appearance is closely tied to Noah’s disappearance. <b>His presence felt like a new opportunity, we grow older and have to let go of old things to embrace the new.</b> Also, I freaking loved his character and he was such a great way to display more of Gansey’s development. But yes, he should have been introduced earlier, agreed.<br /><br /><b><u>Glendower is dead what WHAT?? Then who is the third sleeper??</u></b><br />So, I’ve seen many people hating the fact that Glendower is dead. They felt unsatisfied, betrayed, lead astray. And again, I get it. But I personally thought it was the best choice Maggie could have made. A part of me always knew they wouldn’t be able to wake Glendower, I just wasn’t sure why. <br />So why do I think it was the best option? For me, <b>Gansey was the third sleeper</b>. Throughout the series, Gansey is often referred to as a king. Gansey was the king that was sleeping and woken, both literally (because he was resurrected twice) and figuratively, in the way that he was somewhat lost and didn’t know what to do with his life. <b>Through this whole journey he finds the meaning of his life (which can be seen as a symbolic awakening) and ultimately realises that he does not have to chase down a myth in order to change his life and become what he wants to be.</b> Gansey and the gang were chasing an impossible dream, but along the way discovered that they were the ones holding the magic all along. <i>You are Gansey’s magicians.</i> <br />So who was the king who granted the favour? Ronan. Ronan was the one who dreamt up Cabeswater and asked it to give up its life to resurrect Gansey. <b>Ultimately, they were all the kings of their own lives. We have the power to change our destinies and don’t need to wait around for a Welsh king to swoop in and change us.</b><br /><br /><b><u>Random characters and other bits and pieces</u></b> <br />*sigh* Yes, I agree, some of it felt unnecessary but I just loved the new elements too much to be annoyed by them? Continually introducing new characters is such a Maggie thing to do and I can’t possibly fault her for it since I enjoyed all of it so much.<br /><br /><b><u>The plot felt too predictable</u></b><br />As I said earlier: this book isn’t about all the crazy plot twists. There is so much foreshadowing, Maggie doesn’t <i>want</i> the plot to be unpredictable. <b>This series isn’t about what happens, it’s about how it happens.</b><br /><br /><b><u>The ending is a cop-out? The magic system was bent to accommodate the plot?</u></b><br />Well, I can see where this is coming from but I have to disagree. The ending of this book did not feel like a cop-out to me. <b>All the characters had to make real sacrifices and the solutions came from within themselves rather than some outside magical source.</b> None of it was easy and there was no real magic system to begin with. Everything in this series is weird and somewhat unexplainable, why would the ending be an exception to that? It’s about the journey, not the destination.<br /><br /><b><u>Nothing was clear enough! I’m confused! I want answers! GAHHHHHH</u></b><br />I get you so much, honestly. Part of me wants answers too. But it’s Maggie Stiefvater. Did you really expect her to give you a clear explanation for everything that happens? That’s just not her style. These remaining questions don’t exist because Maggie was lazy. They are purposeful and exist because she created something so full of wonder that does not have to and should not be explained fully.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There is so much more to say but this review is already much too long. Please, PLEASE discuss with me in the comments (just include spoiler tags). I need to talk about this series to everyone. <br /><br /><b>Overall, I'm not giving <i>The Raven King</i> five stars because I think the book is flawless. I'm giving it five stars because despite its flaws, I still consider it one of my best reads of 2016 and found it too good to give it anything lower.</b><br /><br /><b>Depending on where you begin the story, it was about a little book called <i>The Raven Boys</i>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13417793469173554151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2254923376" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407136646" href="/book/show/25394092-the-raven-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=supernatural-paranormal">supernatural-paranormal</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2254923376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13772551987006398201"><i> “He was a book, and he was holding his final pages, and he wanted to get to the end to find out how it went, and he didn’t want it to be over.” </i><br/><br/>Exactly how I felt while reading the final instalment of The Raven Cycle. I’m so sad that it is over, but my heart feels so full from all the characters and the drama of this series! <br/><br/>As the search for Glendower draws to its final conclusion, Cabeswater is under threat and a demon threatens to destroy the lives of the gang. <br/><br/><i> “The darkness wasn’t just in </i></span>
  <span id="freeText13772551987006398201" style="display:none"><i> “He was a book, and he was holding his final pages, and he wanted to get to the end to find out how it went, and he didn’t want it to be over.” </i><br /><br />Exactly how I felt while reading the final instalment of The Raven Cycle. I’m so sad that it is over, but my heart feels so full from all the characters and the drama of this series! <br /><br />As the search for Glendower draws to its final conclusion, Cabeswater is under threat and a demon threatens to destroy the lives of the gang. <br /><br /><i> “The darkness wasn’t just in the tunnel; it was inside him.” </i><br /><br />The darkest of the four books, there were times when I felt these characters spoke to my soul. I could relate to their fears and their love for each other. <br /><br /><i> “It was the gnawing suspicion that you were leavable, that you were too much trouble, that you were better off dead.” </i><br /><br />Blue, Gansey, Noah, Ronan and Adam feel like family, and I loved watching them grow, and their struggles felt like my own struggles. There are plenty of villains, and magic and wonderfulness!<br /><br /><i> “Sometimes it wasn’t about saving yourself, it was about holding out for long enough until someone else could save you.” </i><br /><br />Maggie’s writing style is phenomenal, her descriptions and characterisations unlike anything I’ve ever read! Thank goodness there is more to come from her or I don’t know how I’d cope! <br /><br /><i> “If you can’t be unafraid, Henry said, be afraid and happy.” </i></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3515791275?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Unknown Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Unknown Reviews" href="/user/show/116523065-unknown-reviews">Unknown Reviews</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116523065-unknown-reviews?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>
